Nay v. Dep't of Human Servs.


SC S062978


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 668; 385 P.3d 1001; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 791


November 9, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
December 15, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CA A150722. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* On Judicial Review of Department of Human Services Administrative Rules OAR 461-135-0832 and OAR 461-135-0835. 267 Ore. App. 240, 340 P3d 720 (2014).


Nay v. Dep't of Human Servs., 267 Ore. App. 240, 340 P.3d 720, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1613 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed in part and vacated in part. The rule amendments to OAR 461-135-0832(10)(b)(B)(viii) (2010) and OAR 461-135-0835 (1)(e)(B)(iii) (2010) are held invalid.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Petitioner Department of Human Services' (department) amendments to rules on recovering Medicaid benefits from a recipient's estate were invalid under Or. Rev. Stat. § 183.400(4)(b) because they did not incorporate limits of laws they supposedly effectuated but allowed recovery based on unrelated legal criteria, as they used broader criteria than the marital dissolution statute, allowing a recovery where Or. Rev. Stat. § 107.105(1)(f)(E) would not, they did not lead to the same estate recovery as the elective share statutes in Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 114.600 to 114.725, and allowed a recovery where those statutes did not, let the department recover for transfers without adequate consideration where Or. Rev. Stat. § 416.350(2) did not, and had a different standard than Or. Rev. Stat. § 411.630(2) for recovery due to transfers with intent to hinder or prevent estate recovery.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed in part and vacated in part.

 

2 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Barrett v. Peters


SC S063743 (Control), SC S063744


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 445; 383 P.3d 813; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 682


June 14, 2016, Argued and Submitted 
October 20, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 13C20437; CA A155789; CC 13C23141; CA A156271. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Courtland Geyer, Judge. 274 Ore. App. 237, 360 P3d 638 (2015); 274 Ore. App. 251, 360 P3d 646 (2015).


Barrett v. Peters, 274 Ore. App. 251, 360 P.3d 646, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 1202 (2015)
Barrett v. Peters, 274 Ore. App. 237, 360 P.3d 638, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 1203 (2015)



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Court of Appeals are affirmed. The judgments of the circuit court are reversed, and the cases are remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where petitioner was incarcerated in Oregon for aggravated murder, his transfer to Florida did not prohibit him from bringing claims that his confinement in Florida violated his constitutional rights because the Interstate Corrections Compact, Or. Rev. Stat. § 421.245, supplemented the habeas statutes and preserved his right to participate in any proceedings in which he could have participated if he were incarcerated in Oregon; [2]-Inmates incarcerated outside of Oregon as the result of transfer under the Interstate Corrections Compact, Or. Rev. Stat. § 421.245, are permitted to file claims for habeas corpus in Oregon; [3]-Petitioner alleged cognizable violations of the state and federal constitutions; [4]-The Director of the Oregon Department of Corrections was the proper defendant in the habeas petitions.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

State v. Ghim


SC S063021


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 425; 381 P.3d 789; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 680


November 10, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
October 13, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC C111491CR; CA A152065. On appeal from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* On appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Gayle A. Nachtigal, Judge. 267 Ore. App. 435, 340 P3d 753 (2014).


State v. Ghim, 267 Ore. App. 435, 340 P.3d 753, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1702 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Administrative subpoenas issued by the Oregon Department of Consumer and Business Services (DCBS) under Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.315(1), 192.596(1), (2) did not violate defendant's Or. Const. art. I, § 9 rights because the subpoenas fell squarely within DCBS's statutory authority under Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.245(1),.255(1), (4) to investigate the sale of unregistered securities in Oregon.


OUTCOME: Decision and judgment affirmed.

 

4 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Davidson


SC S063387 (Control), SC S063480


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 370; 380 P.3d 963; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 610


May 9, 2016, Argued and Submitted 
September 22, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: (S063387) (Control). (S063480). CC 11C43121; CA A150292. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* On appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Dale W. Penn, Judge. 271 Ore. App. 719, 353 P3d 2 (2015).


State v. Davidson, 271 Ore. App. 719, 353 P.3d 2, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 770 (2015)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's sentences under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.719(1) were unconstitutionally disproportionate under Or. Const. art. I, § 16 because the gravity of the offense of public indecency under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.465(1)(c) was relatively minor in comparison with the majority of the other sex offenses identified in Or. Rev. Stat. § 163A.005(5); where a criminal defendant--even an incorrigible one--has a criminal history that includes no offenses more serious than public indecency (and no other misconduct that otherwise supports a conclusion that he or she poses a significant physical danger to society), a sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole for public indecency is unconstitutionally disproportionate; [2]-Court did not err in declining to give the requested attempt instruction under Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.405 because the instruction would not have advanced defendant's theory of the case.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed, sentences reversed, and remanded.

State v. Sokell


SC S063607


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 392; 380 P.3d 975; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 611


May 9, 2016, Argued and Submitted 
September 22, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC C131532CR; CA A156133. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* On appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Andrew Erwin, Judge. 273 Ore. App. 654, 362 P3d 251.


State v. Sokell, 273 Ore. App. 654, 362 P.3d 251, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 1093 (2015)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A presumptive sentence of life imprisonment without the possibility of parole, imposed pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.719(1), was not constitutionally disproportionate under Or. Const. art. I, § 16 on a conviction for first-degree sexual abuse because the victim was a young child targeted and fondled by defendant at a public library, the victim suffered severe trauma, and defendant had an extensive history of committing sexual abuse offenses against young children.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals and judgment of the circuit court affirmed.

 

6 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Nascimento


SC S063197


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 28; 379 P.3d 484; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 468; 166 Lab. Cas. (CCH) P61,724


November 12, 2015, Argued and submitted 
July 21, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 09FE0092, CA A147290. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Jefferson County Circuit Court, George W. Neilson, Judge. 268 Ore. App. 718, 343 P3d 654 (2015).


State v. Nascimento, 268 Ore. App. 718, 343 P.3d 654, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 121 (2015)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's use of her employer's lottery terminal to print Keno tickets for herself without paying for them was not "without authorization" for purposes of a computer crime conviction; defendant was authorized to use the computer to print Keno tickets, and the fact that her conduct violated her employer's policy did not make her computer use "unauthorized"; [2]-The phrase "without authorization" in Or. Rev. Stat. § 164.377(4) applies to the use or access of the computer; an employee's authorized use of an employer's computer does not become "without authorization" simply because the employee used the computer for a purpose not permitted by the employer's personnel or computer use policies.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed; judgment of the circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

 

7 of 770 DOCUMENTS


E. Or. Mining Ass'n v. Dep't of Envtl. Quality


SC S063549


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


360 Ore. 10; 376 P.3d 288; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 463


June 9, 2016, Submitted on the briefs 
July 14, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by E. Or. Mining Ass'n v. Dep't of Envtl. Quality, 2017 Ore. App. LEXIS 711 (Or. Ct. App., June 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 10C24263, 11C19071; CA A156161. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Courtland Geyer, Judge. 273 Ore. App. 259, 361 P3d 38 (2015).


E. Or. Mining Ass'n v. Dep't of Envtl. Quality, 273 Ore. App. 259, 361 P.3d 38, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 976 (Aug. 19, 2015)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The miners relied on the Uniform Declaratory Judgment Act to challenge the validity of a settlement agreement concerning the implementation of the 2010 permit, and any judicial decision as to that challenge would not affect the rights of any of the parties, and the permit to which the settlement agreement otherwise would have applied had expired; [2]-The miners' challenge was of the sort that was likely to evade review within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.175(3) because the case had become moot twice, even after the parties requested, and were denied, expedited consideration; [3]-Whether to limit judicial review was a matter of discretion under the statute; [4]-The enactment of the moratorium did not preclude the exercise of discretion to issue a judgment on the claims at issue.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and remanded.

 

8 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Althouse


SC S062909


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


359 Ore. 668; 375 P.3d 475; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 365


September 14, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
June 16, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 11C48471; CA A152626. On review from the Court of Appeals. [**1] *


* On appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Lindsay Partridge, Judge. 266 Ore. App. 548, 339 P.3d 470 (2014).


State v. Althouse, 266 Ore. App. 548, 339 P.3d 470, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1423 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Where defendant was convicted of felony public indecency after previously having been convicted of three other felony sex crimes, his sentence to life imprisonment without the possibility of parole pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.719(1) was not constitutionally disproportionate to his criminal history under Or. Const. art. I, § 16; [2]-Given the seriousness of defendant's repeated sexual misconduct and the danger that it forecasts for others, imposing a presumptive life sentence in response to defendant's pattern of criminal behavior did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 16; [3]-Defendant's sentence did not violate the Eighth Amendment's prohibition against cruel and unusual punishment.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

9 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Horton v. Or. Health & Sci. Univ.


SC S061992


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


359 Ore. 168; 376 P.3d 998; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 320


November 6, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
May 5, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 1108-11209. On direct appeal from the judgment of the Multnomah County Circuit Court. [***1] *


* On appeal from a limited judgment, Jerry B. Hodson, Judge. Multnomah County Circuit Court, January 6, 2014.


Horton v. Or. Health & Sci. Univ., 277 Ore. App. 821, 373 P.3d 1158, 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 504 (2016)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a medical malpractice suit involving a state employee doctor, the Tort Claims Act, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 30.271(3)(a) and 30.265(1), which limited the doctor's tort liability, such that the available damages were insufficient to fully compensate the patient, the Act did not violate the remedy clause, Or. Const. art. I, § 10, because the remedy clause did not preclude the legislature from altering common law duties and remedies, and the Act properly accommodated the state's constitutionally recognized interest in sovereign immunity with the plaintiff's right to a remedy; [2]-Applying the Act's limit to a jury's damages award did not violate the right to a jury trial in civil cases in Or. Const. art. I, § 17 and Or. Const. art. VII, § 3 because the court was not reexamining a fact found by the jury, but applying a legal statutory limit to the facts that the jury had found.


OUTCOME: Decision reversed; case remanded.

 

10 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turnidge


SC S059156


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


359 Ore. 507; 373 P.3d 138; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 316


January 15, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
May 5, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Turnidge, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 523 (Or., Aug. 5, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turnidge v. Oregon, 2016 U.S. LEXIS 7304 (U.S., Dec. 5, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 08C53913. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentences of death imposed by the Marion County Circuit Court. Thomas M. Hart, Judge.
State v. Turnidge, 359 Ore. 364, 374 P.3d 853, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 319 (2016)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentences of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's death penalty case, evidence of defendant's long-standing anti-government sentiments was relevant under Or. Evid. Code 401 because his professed desire to kill police officers, and form an anti-government militia logically tended to support the State's theory; the evidence was a basis on which the jury could conclude that defendant spent time visualizing acting on those hostilities in violent ways; [2]-The prosecutor properly pointed to penalty-phase evidence of defendant's past threats to kill others, as well as to defendant's zeal to form an anti-government militia; in that context the prosecutor was referring to defendant's dangerousness in terms of his willingness to commit crimes based on his violent ideologies and his desire to influence others to commit crimes in pursuit of those same ideologies.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

11 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Turnidge


SC S059155


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


359 Ore. 364; 374 P.3d 853; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 319


June 17, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
May 5, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by State v. Turnidge, 359 Ore. 507, 373 P.3d 138, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 316 (2016)
Reconsideration denied by State v. Turnidge, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 511 (Or., Aug. 5, 2016)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Turnidge v. Or., 2017 U.S. LEXIS 232 (U.S., Jan. 9, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 08C51758. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentences of death imposed by the Marion County Circuit Court. Thomas. M. Hart, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentences of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-As a joint trial of defendant and a co-defendant was not "clearly inappropriate" under the circumstances, Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.060(1), the trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion to sever; [2]-As the record supported the trial court's determination that the views of three prospective jurors on the death penalty would interfere with their respective abilities to follow the law, the trial court did not abuse its discretion in excusing them under the Sixth Amendment; [3]-The trial court's decision to destroy juror questionnaires after voir dire was completed, while ill-advised, did not prejudice him; [4]-Evidence of defendant's anti-government views and hostile attitude toward law enforcement was relevant to issues being tried; [5]-The trial court did not err in denying defendant's motion for acquittal on the ground that the State failed to prove intent.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction and sentences of death were affirmed.

 

12 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Nearman v. Rosenblum


SC S063787 Control SC S063789


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 818; 371 P.3d 1186; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 173



March 24, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Later proceeding at Nearman v. Rosenblum, 359 Ore. 40, 370 P.3d 1253, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 248 (Or., Apr. 8, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] On petitions to review ballot title filed January 5, 2016; considered and under advisement February 23, 2016.



DISPOSITION: The ballot title is referred to the Attorney General for modification.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In stating that the application of a proposed ballot measure that would change current voter registration methods for federal, state, and local elections in Oregon by requiring in-person registration, the Attorney General's caption did not substantially comply with the requirement in Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.035(2)(a) that the caption reasonably identify the subject of the measure; [2]-In addition, the summary failed to state a major effect of the measure because it did not state that, by its terms, the measure would apply to federal elections; [3]-Accordingly, both the caption and the summary had to be modified to identify that subject and major effect; [4]-The reference in the "yes" result statement to "immigration verification" was inaccurate and misleading, and the "yes" vote result statement had to be modified to remove it.


OUTCOME: Ballot title referred to the Attorney General for modification.

 

13 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Dep't of Human Servs. v. T.L. (In re M.L.)


SC S063204


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 679; 369 P.3d 1159; 2016 Ore. LEXIS 136


November 12, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
March 3, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Dep't of Human Servs. v. T.L. (In re M.L.), 287 Ore. App. 753, 2017 Ore. App. LEXIS 1066 (Sept. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 110440J02; CC 110441J02; CA A155300 (Control); CA A155301. On review from the Court of Appeals.* [***1] .


* Appeal from Clackamas County Circuit Court, Douglas V. Van Dyk, Judge. 269 Ore. App. 454, 344 P3d 1123 (2015).


Dep't of Human Servs. v. T.L. (In re M. L.), 269 Ore. App. 454, 344 P.3d 1123, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 265 (Mar. 4, 2015)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-When counsel has been appointed in a permanency proceeding under Or. Rev. Stat. § 419B.476, and a change of plan from return to parent to a permanent plan of guardianship or another planned permanent living arrangement is ordered, counsel must have been adequate, with adequacy determined using a standard of fundamental fairness; [2]-A parent can raise the claim of inadequate assistance of counsel for the first time on direct appeal; [3]-Or. Rev. Stat. § 419B.923 does not require that a parent raise an ineffective assistance of counsel claim in the first instance in the juvenile court; [4]-A more complete evidentiary record was necessary to determine whether counsel was ineffective in failing to appear at a permanency hearing because the record did not reveal whether there was a reasonable explanation or whether the parent was prejudiced by counsel's absence.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

14 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Alderwoods (Or.), Inc.


SC S062766


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 501; 366 P.3d 316; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 956


June 16, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
December 31, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Alderwoods (Or.), Inc., 2016 Ore. LEXIS 227 (Or., Apr. 7, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC C085449CV; CA A146317. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Thomas W. Kohl, Judge.265 Ore. App 572, 336 P3d 1047 (2014)


State v. Alderwoods (Or.), Inc., 265 Ore. App. 572, 336 P.3d 1047, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1301 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-An owner of a corner lot abutting a highway had a common-law right of access that was not specific to a particular location but entitled the owner to reasonable access to its property from the highway, subject to the state's interest in the safety of the highway; [2]-The removal of two driveways did not constitute a taking under Or. Const. art. I, § 18 because it was uncontested that the state acted to promote highway safety and the owner retained unimpaired access by two other driveways located a short distance from the intersection with the highway, which was reasonable access as a matter of law; [3]-Evidence of diminished value as a result of the removal of the driveways was properly excluded as irrelevant in a condemnation action to acquire a temporary construction easement; [4]-As a procedural statute, Or. Rev. Stat. § 374.035 granted the owner no substantive rights.


OUTCOME: Decision and judgment affirmed.

 

15 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Gonzalez-Valenzuela


SC S061751


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 451; 365 P.3d 116; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 928


May 7, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
December 24, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC C100316CR; CA A146278. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Steven L. Price, Judge. 258 Ore. App. 263, 303 P.3d 1096 (2013).


State v. Gonzalez-Valenzuela, 258 Ore. App. 263, 308 P.3d 1096, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 1007 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Illegal drug possession could constitute unlawful activity involving controlled substances for purposes of a child-endangerment offense under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.575(1)(b), construed in light of the definitions of "possess" in Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.015(9) and "act" in Or. Rev. Stat. § 161.085(5), because activity encompassed not only culpable action but also culpable inaction in failing to dispose of the drugs; [2]-A brief isolated incident of drug activity was legally insufficient to establish that a place was one where unlawful activity involving controlled substances was maintained or conducted, which meant a principal or substantial use of the place was to facilitate unlawful drug activity; [3]-Defendant was entitled to a judgment of acquittal because her possession of drugs while in a car with her daughters was no more than a brief isolated incident of drug activity.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

17 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Agee


SC S059530


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 325; 364 P.3d 971; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 890


April 23, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
December 3, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On reconsideration by, Modified by, Adhered to State v. Agee, 358 Ore. 749, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 168 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 09C41224. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by Marion County Circuit Court. Pamela L. Abernethy, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction is affirmed. The sentence of death is vacated, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's death sentence after he was convicted of aggravated murder was improper under U.S. Const. amend. VIII and Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.150(1)(a), because, allowing the trial court's ruling to stand would create an unacceptable risk that a person with intellectual disability would be executed; [2]-Even though the trial court's ruling comported with the published standards existing at the time that the court ruled, the trial court did not apply now-current medical standards in determining that defendant had not met his burden of proof to show that he had an intellectual disability.


OUTCOME: Conviction affirmed; sentence of death vacated; case remanded.

 

18 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hickman


SC S061896 (Control), SC S061902


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


358 Ore. 1; 358 P.3d 987; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 720


October 8, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
October 8, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Hickman, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 876 (Or., Nov. 30, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC CR1001094; CA A150127; CC CR1001093; CA A150126; On review of an order of the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Court of Appeals Order of Summary Affirmance dated August 20, 2013. Appeal from Clackamas County Circuit Court, Robert D. Herndon, Judge.


State v. Hickman, 2013 Ore. LEXIS 880 (Or., Oct. 28, 2013)
State v. Hickman, 2013 Ore. LEXIS 879 (Or., Oct. 28, 2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant parents, who were members of the Followers of Christ Church, were properly convicted of second degree manslaughter based on their criminal negligence in declining to seek medical treatment for their premature infant, who died about nine hours after being born, because Or. Const. art. I, §§ 2, 3, did not require the state to prove defendants knew an unlawful result would follow from conduct that was motivated by a sincerely held religious belief; [2]-The court disavowed Meltebeke v. Bureau of Labor and Industries, 322 Ore. 132, 903 P2d 351 (1995) to the extent it relied on Smith v. Employment Division, 301 Ore. 209, 721 P2d 445 (1986) for the holding that an employer had to know his religiously motivated conduct had a harassing effect on an employee before the employer could, consistent with free exercise principles, be civilly sanctioned for the harassment.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals and judgment of the circuit court affirmed.

 

19 of 770 DOCUMENTS


City of Seattle v. Dep't of Revenue


SC S061813


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 718; 357 P.3d 979; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 664


November 3, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
September 11, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: TC-RD 4946, 4957, TC-RD 4959, TC-RD 4958. On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court.* [***1] Henry C. Breithaupt, Judge.


* 21 OTR 269 (2013).


City of Seattle v. Dep't of Revenue, 21 OTR 269, 2013 Ore. Tax LEXIS 163 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Summary judgment was properly awarded to the Oregon Department of Revenue because the Washington taxpayers' interest in electrical transmission capacity purchased from the power administration and used to transmit electricity over the northwest's federally administered power grid could be taxed by the Department as a property interest "held" by the taxpayers under Or. Rev. Stat. § 307.060 (1995); [2]-The Oregon Legislature's repeal of a 2005 property tax exemption previously benefitting the taxpayers did not violate Or. Const. art. IV, § 18; Oregon Senate Bill 495 "raised revenue" within the meaning of that provision.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

20 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Lane


SC S062045


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 619; 355 P.3d 914; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 576


September 18, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
August 6, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 07C49819; CA A148507. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Joseph V. Ochoa, Judge. 260 Ore. App. 549, 318 P3d 750 (2014).


State v. Lane, 260 Ore. App. 549, 318 P.3d 750, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Or. Admin. R. 213-012-0040(2)(a) (requiring that, if a defendant with multiple terms of probation commits a single probation violation, any resulting terms of incarceration must be imposed concurrently, not consecutively) runs afoul of Or. Const. art. I, § 44(1)(b); imposing terms of incarceration as a sanction upon probation revocation amounts to "sentencing for crimes" within the meaning of art. I, § 44; [2]-Following a single violation of a no-drinking condition of probation, the trial court properly imposed consecutive sentences for defendant's four convictions, involving four separate victims, for encouraging child sex abuse.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed; judgment of the circuit court affirmed.

Verduzco v. State


SC S062339


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 553; 355 P.3d 902; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 518


March 12, 2015, Argued and Submitted, at the University of Oregon School of Law, Eugene 
July 30, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Verduzco v. State, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 712 (Or., Oct. 8, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC CV110467; CA A153165. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Yamhill County Circuit Court, Ronald W. Stone, Judge. Order of Summary Affirmance, May 6, 2014.


Verduzco v. State, 355 Ore. 879, 333 P.3d 333, 2014 Ore. LEXIS 566 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because petitioner raised his claim, that trial counsel provided inadequate assistance when she failed to advise him accurately of the immigration consequences of his plea, in his first postconviction relief petition, Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.550(3) barred the grounds for relief in his second postconviction petition; the escape clause did not preclude him from relitigating only those grounds for relief that he was certain he could win when he filed his first post-conviction petition but, rather, it precluded him raising those grounds of relief that he could not reasonably have raised in his first petition.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

 

22 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Couey v. Atkins


SC S061650


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 460; 355 P.3d 866; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 516


June 24, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
July 16, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 10C14484; CA A148473. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Claudia M. Burton, Judge. 257 Ore. App 434, 306 P.3d 778 (2013).


Couey v. Brown, 257 Ore. App. 434, 306 P.3d 778, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 827 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A declaratory action challenging the restriction in Or. Rev. Stat. § 250.048(9) on volunteer work by registered paid initiative petition signature collectors became moot when the plaintiff's registration expired because any future harm was speculative; [2]-An overbreadth claim did not excuse the standing requirement; [3]-The action was not justiciable under Or. Rev. Stat. § 246.910; [4]-Although moot, the action could proceed under Or. Rev. Stat. § 14.175 because a similar challenge likely would evade judicial review, even if expedited consideration or certification under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 19.405(1), 246.910(4) might be available in some cases; [5]-Section 14.175 was constitutional because Or. Const. art. VII (Amended), § 1 had no justiciability requirement that would preclude courts from deciding moot public action cases or those involving matters of public interest.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

State v. Jimenez


SC S062473


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 417; 353 P.3d 1227; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 441


March 12, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
July 9, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 110241478; CA A148796. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Christopher J. Marshall, Judge. 263 Ore. App. 150, 326 P3d 1222 (2014).


State v. Jimenez, 263 Ore. App. 150, 326 P.3d 1222, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 684 (2014)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Conviction of unlawful possession of a firearm under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.250(1)(a) was subject to reversal because the State did not establish that the trooper's weapons inquiry was reasonably related to his traffic investigation when he stopped defendant for jaywalking under Or. Rev. Stat. § 814.020(1), (3); when a law enforcement conducts a traffic investigation, Or. Const. art. I, § 9 does not permit the law enforcement officer to make an inquiry whether the person has any weapons on him or her as a matter of routine and in the absence of circumstances that indicate danger to the officer or members of the public.


OUTCOME: Decision affirmed, judgment reversed, and case remanded.

Moro v. State


S061431S061452 (Control), S061454, S061475,S061860


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 167; 351 P.3d 1; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 277


October 14, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
April 30, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Moro v. State, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 692 (Or., Oct. 8, 2015)
Costs and fees proceeding at Moro v. State, 358 Ore. 375, 364 P.3d 325, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 895 (2015)
Costs and fees proceeding at Moro v. State, 360 Ore. 467, 384 P.3d 504, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 685 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: Moro v. State, 354 Ore. 657, 320 P.3d 539, 2014 Ore. LEXIS 11 (2014)



DISPOSITION: * Senate Bill 822, signed into law May 6, 2013, and Senate Bill 861, signed into law October 8, 2013.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 238.362(3), tax offsets provided by former law were not terms of the statutory Oregon Public Employee Retirement System (PERS) unilateral contract and thus could be changed without an Oregon Contract Clause, Or. Const. art. I, § 21, violation; [2]-The cost of living adjustment (COLA) provisions of Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 238.360 (2011), 238A.210 (2011) were contractual PERS terms and could be changed only prospectively, consistent with Or. Rev. Stat. § 238A.470 and the Contract Clause; [3]-Case law implying a term of irrevocability did not apply because the COLA benefit did not impose conditions on acceptance taking time to complete; [4]-Supplemental payment provisions that could not be severed from unconstitutional application of the amended legislation because they otherwise would not have been enacted were void under Or. Rev. Stat. § 174.040(2).


OUTCOME: Legislation declared unconstitutional in part.

State v. Williams


CC 08CR0707; CA A145644; SC S061769


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


357 Ore. 1; 346 P.3d 455; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 183


June 23, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
March 19, 2015, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. Williams, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 432 (Or., June 18, 2015)
On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by State v. Williams, 276 Ore. App. 688, 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 223 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Josephine County Circuit Court, Pat Wolke, Judge. 258 Ore App 106, 308 P.3d 330 (2013).


State v. Williams, 258 Ore. App. 106, 308 P.3d 330, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 956 (2013)


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a prosecution for child sexual abuse, subjecting proffered "other acts" evidence to Or. Evid. Code 403 balancing was held to be a due process requirement, as it was the only way to ensure that the admission of such evidence was not unfairly prejudicial; [2]-The trial court did not err in finding that the children's underwear was relevant in a trial for first-degree sexual abuse, as defendant's sexual purpose was an element of the charged crimes, the State was required to prove that defendant acted with a sexual desire that was aroused or gratified by contact with children, and the underwear allowed the jury to infer that defendant had a sexual interest in children.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

State v. Mazzola


SC S062126


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 804; 345 P.3d 424; 2015 Ore. LEXIS 176


October 9, 2014, Argued and submitted, at La Grande High School, La Grande, Oregon. 
March 5, 2015, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: On review from the Court of Appeals.* [***1] CC 101198M; CA A148224.


* Appeal from Josephine County Circuit Court, Pat Wolke, Judge. 260 Ore. App. 378, 317 P3d 360 (2013).


State v. Mazzola, 260 Ore. App. 378, 317 P.3d 360, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 1505 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Because defendant was subject to arrest for driving under the influence pursuant to Or. Rev. Stat. § 813.010, and because the administration of the challenged field sobriety tests was reasonable in time, scope, and intensity, the evidence of exigent circumstances was sufficient to make the warrantless administration of those tests constitutionally permissible; the tests did not intrude into defendant's body, rather, they assessed her coordination, balance, and motor skills and secured observational evidence of defendant's physical impairment due to the use of controlled substances.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

 

28 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Kennedy v. Wheeler


SC S061836


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 518; 341 P.3d 728; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 937


September 16, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
December 11, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC CV080512; CA A149019. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Yamhill County Circuit Court, Carroll J. Tichenor, Judge. 258 Ore. App. 343, 309 P3d 196 (2013).


Kennedy v. Wheeler, 258 Ore. App. 343, 309 P.3d 196, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 1018 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a collision case, the jury's verdict met the requirements of Or. Const. art. VII, § 5(7) (amended) and Or. R. Civ. P. 59 G(2) because the jurors unanimously agreed that defendant caused damage to plaintiff, and at least nine also agreed to award specific amounts of economic and noneconomic damages; it was not necessary that the same nine jurors agree on the amounts of economic and noneconomic damages awarded; [2]-The law of the case doctrine did not preclude consideration of the issue, even if the trial court, when instructed the jury, made a deliberate ruling or decision that the same nine jurors had to agree on the specific amount of economic and noneconomic damages awarded.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals reversed; judgment of the circuit court affirmed.

State v. McAnulty


SC S059476


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 432; 338 P.3d 653; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 809


March 20, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
October 30, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by State v. McAnulty, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 22 (Or., Jan. 15, 2015)
US Supreme Court certiorari denied by McAnulty v. Or., 2015 U.S. LEXIS 5961 (U.S., Oct. 5, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CC 200927457. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Lane County Circuit Court. Kip W. Leonard, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In defendant's death penalty case, the scope of review limitations contained in Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.050 and 138.222 did not apply to the Oregon Supreme Court's automatic and direct review of a conviction and sentence of death under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.012(1); [2]-Defendant unequivocally invoked her right to remain silent under Or. Const. art. I, § 12 and the detectives violated her rights when they persisted in questioning her after her second and third invocations; as a result, defendant's statements from the first interrogation should have been suppressed and were improperly admitted during the penalty-phase proceeding; [3]-The error in admitting defendant's statements was harmless because the improperly admitted evidence was duplicative; moreover, in her plea petition, defendant admitted to the "intentional maiming and torturing" of the victim.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

Comcast Corp. v. Dep't of Revenue

SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 282; 337 P.3d 768; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 748


January 8, 2013, Argued and submitted 
October 2, 2014, Decided

On remand at Comcast Corp. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2015 Ore. Tax LEXIS 43 (Or. T.C., Apr. 21, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: TC 4909. On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. [***1] *


* 20 OTR 319 (2011).


Comcast Corp. v. Dep't of Revenue, 20 OTR 319, 2011 Ore. Tax LEXIS 321 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Tax Court is reversed, and the case is remanded to that court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Both the cable television and internet access services provided by the taxpayer qualified as "data transmission services" within the meaning of Or. Rev. Stat. § 308.505(2) (2007) and were, therefore, communication services subject to central assessment under Or. Rev. Stat. § 308.515(1)(h); "data transmission service" was interpreted to extend to any service that provided the means for the transmission of electronically coded information between computers or computer-like devices.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Doyle v. City of Medford


SC S061463


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 336; 337 P.3d 797; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 701


March 13, 2014, Argued and submitted at the University of Oregon Law School, Eugene, Oregon. 
October 2, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Doyle v. City of Medford, 2015 Ore. LEXIS 122 (Or., Feb. 19, 2015)
On remand at, Remanded by Doyle v. City of Medford, 271 Ore. App. 458, 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 657 (2015)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 080137L7; CA A147497. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Jackson County Circuit Court, Mark S. Schiveley, Judge. 256 Ore App 625, 303 P3d 346 (2013).


Doyle v. City of Medford, 256 Ore. App. 625, 303 P.3d 346, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 536 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The case is remanded to that court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Or. Rev. Stat. § 243.303(2), which requires that local governments make available to retired employees the health care insurance coverage provided to current employees, where possible, does not create a private right of action for a violation; [2]-Judicial creation of a tort-based right of action was neither appropriate for promoting the policy of the statute nor needed to ensure its effectiveness; [3]-The Declaratory Judgments Act provided a sufficient avenue, in the absence of a right to a tort action, for retirees to assert that their city employer failed, as required by § 243.303(2), to provide the same health care insurance coverage provided to current employees.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

32 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Unger


SC S060888


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 59; 333 P.3d 1009; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 635


September 17, 2013, Argued and Submitted 
August 28, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by State v. Unger, 276 Ore. App. 445, 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 129 (2016)


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 09C42443; CA A144192. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* Appeal from Marion Court Circuit Court, Thomas M. Hart, Judge. 252 Ore. App. 478, 287 P3d 1196 (2012).


State v. Unger, 252 Ore. App. 478, 287 P.3d 1196, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 1163 (2012)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Under Or. Const. art. I, § 9, an unlawful entry into defendant's backyard to reach his back door did not taint a subsequent consent to search because the detectives did not exploit the unlawful entry to obtain consent; their purpose was to contact the homeowner to ask for permission to search, not to search for incriminating evidence near the back door, and the conduct was not egregious; [2]-When a defendant has established that an illegal stop or search occurred and challenges the validity of a subsequent consent to a search, the state must demonstrate that the consent was voluntary and that the voluntary consent was not the product of police exploitation of the illegality; courts must consider the totality of the circumstances, including the nature of the illegal conduct and its purpose and flagrancy (disavowing in part State v. Hall, 339 Or. 7, 115 P.3d 908 (2005)).


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

 

33 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Washington


SC S058490


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


355 Ore. 612; 330 P.3d 596; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 480


June 4, 2013, Argued and Submitted 
June 19, 2014, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: US Supreme Court certiorari denied by Washington v. Oregon, 2014 U.S. LEXIS 7658 (U.S., Nov. 17, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC CR0701950. On automatic and direct review of the judgment of conviction and sentence of death imposed by the Clackamas County Circuit Court. Thomas Rastetter, Judge.



DISPOSITION: The judgment of conviction and sentence of death are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a capital murder trial under Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.095, the non-accomplice evidence was sufficient to corroborate accomplice testimony, in part because witnesses saw the accomplice leave the victim's apartment, heard gunshots from the apartment moments later, and then saw defendant leave the apartment, and cell phone data corroborated the accomplice testimony about defendant's movements; [2]-Wearing a stun device during a trial did not violate defendant's rights in part because the device was not visible to the jury; [3]-Empaneling an anonymous jury did not violate the Sixth Amendment because the record supported findings that defendant had a history of violent crimes and connections with gangs, the courtroom was not secure, defendant posed an escape risk from a courtroom with exits to the street, and defendant could readily overpower security personnel.


OUTCOME: Judgment of conviction and sentence of death affirmed.

Epler & Epler


SC S061818


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


356 Ore. 624; 341 P.3d 742; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 999


June 23, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
May 26, 2014, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY: CC 04C33678; CA A148643. On review from the Court of Appeals. [***1] *


* On appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Dennis J. Graves, Judge. 258 Ore App 464, 309 P3d 1133 (2013).


Epler & Epler, 258 Ore. App. 464, 309 P.3d 1133, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 1103 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded to the circuit court to rule on mother's request to modify parenting time and child support.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The mother was not entitled to the presumption that her decision that the child should return to her custody was in the child's best interest; the mother and father had requested and received court approval of a marital settlement agreement expressing their desire that the grandmother be awarded sole legal and physical custody of their minor child; [2]-The mother was not prejudiced by the trial court's determination that she had not showed a substantial change in circumstances because the court considered whether a change in custody was in the child's best interest; [3]-The child's best interests would not be served by a change in custody because she had lived with the grandmother for the past seven formative years of her life; at the time of the hearing, the mother had visited the child a total of five times.


OUTCOME: Affirmed and remanded.

State v. Babson


SC S060455 (Control); SC S060610, SC S060455 (Control); SC S060376

355 Ore. 383; 326 P.3d 559; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 368


June 13, 2013, Argued and Submitted

PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 09C41582; CA A144037 (Control); CC 09C41583; CA A144037 (Control); CA A144038; CC 09C41584; CA A144037 (Control); CA A144039; CC 09C41593; CA A144037 (Control); CA A144042; CC 09C41594; CA A144037 (Control); CA A144043; CC 09C41581; CA A144037 (Control); CA A144345. On review from the Court of Appeals.*


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Jamese Lou Rhoades, Judge. 249 Ore App 278, 279 P3d 222 (2012).


State v. Babson, 249 Ore. App. 278, 279 P.3d 222, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 461 (2012)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is affirmed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed in part and reversed in part, and the case is remanded for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-A prohibition on overnight use of the steps of the state capitol building between 11:00 p.m. and 7:00 a.m., except in limited circumstances, did not on its face violate Or. I, § 26, protecting free expression and the rights to assemble, instruct representatives, and apply for redress of grievances, because the prohibition was not written in terms directed to the substance of any opinion or subject of communication and was not simply a mirror of a prohibition on words; [2]-The Oregon Debate Clause, Or. Const. art. IV, § 9, did not bar defendant protestors from questioning legislators about enforcement, which is not generally part of the legislative function, of the prohibition, for purposes of their challenges to the constitutionality of the guideline as applied to prosecutions for criminal trespass.


OUTCOME: Decision of the Court of Appeals affirmed; judgment of the circuit court affirmed in part and reversed in part; case remanded for further proceedings.

Dep't of Human Servs. v. S.M. (In re M.M.)


SC S061386 (Control)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


355 Ore. 241; 323 P.3d 947; 2014 Ore. LEXIS 301


November 5, 2013, Argued and Submitted at Franklin High School, Portland, Oregon. 
April 24, 2014, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Dep't of Human Servs. v. S.M., 2014 Ore. LEXIS 454 (Or., June 12, 2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC J110590, J110591, J110592, J110593, J110594, J110595, J110596, J011597; CA A151376 (Control). On review from the Court of Appeals.*


* On appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Julia A. Philbrook, Judge. 256 Ore. App 15, 300 P3d 1254 (2013).


Dep't of Human Servs. v. S.M. (In re M.M.), 256 Ore. App. 15, 300 P.3d 1254, 2013 Ore. App. LEXIS 394 (2013)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgments of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: ISSUE: Whether the legislature gave the Department of Human Services (DHS), in its capacity as either the children's custodian or their guardian, authority to have the children immunized against common childhood diseases. HOLDINGS: [1]-Under Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 419B.372 and 419B.376, DHS had statutory authority as the children's legal guardian to approve their immunization; [2]-Consistently with its own rules, DHS did not make that decision unilaterally, but rather, it notified the juvenile court and sought its concurrence, thereby giving the children's parents the opportunity to voice any objection they had to the proposed procedure and also giving the juvenile court the opportunity to pass on the issue; [3]-DHS's power to make other decisions of substantial legal significance included the power to immunize the wards in its care against common childhood diseases.


OUTCOME: Decision and judgments affirmed.

State v. Moore

December 12, 2013, Filed

State v. Moore, 247 Ore. App. 39, 269 P.3d 72, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 1665 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The order of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's consent was voluntary under Or. Const. art. OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

State v. Savastano


SC S059973


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


354 Ore. 64; 309 P.3d 1083; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 720


September 20, 2012, Argued and Submitted; January 7, 2013, Resubmitted 
September 12, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC C081586CR; CA A141053. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Washington County Circuit Court, Thomas Kohl, Judge. 243 Ore. App. 584, 260 P3d 529, adh'd to on recons, 246 Ore. App. 566, 266 P3d 176 (2011).


State v. Savastano, 243 Ore. App. 584, 260 P.3d 529, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 853 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In an embezzlement case, the prosecutor did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 20 by aggregating the transactions by month, even though the prosecutor's office did not have a policy for aggregating theft transactions, because the prosecutor had a rational basis for his decision (to create a clear organizational outline for the jury) and defendant did not demonstrate differential treatment; [2]-A prosecutor's failure to adopt or adhere to policies does not violate the privileges or immunities provision; a government decision-maker will be in compliance as long as there is a rational explanation for the differential treatment that is reasonably related to the official task or individual situation (overruling State v. Freeland, 295 Or. 367, 667 P.2d 509 (1983)).


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and affirmed the conviction.

41 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Fair


SC S058458


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 588; 302 P.3d 417; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 385


January 11, 2011, Argued and Submitted; January 7, 2013, Resubmitted 
May 31, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 06FE1759AB; CA A136985. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Deschutes County Circuit Court, Alta J. Brady, Judge. 233 Ore. App. 298, 225 P3d 848 (2010).


State v. Fair, 233 Ore. App. 298, 225 P.3d 848, 2010 Ore. App. LEXIS 50 (2010)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: After her motion to suppress evidence was denied, defendant entered a conditional guilty plea to possession of a controlled substance. The Oregon Court of Appeals reversed denial of suppression. The State appealed.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court found that officers' conduct in ordering defendant to step out of her home was a show of authority that significantly intruded on her liberty and amounted to a seizure. The subsequent order to remain on the porch while one officer questioned her immediately followed the order to step out of the house. That second order continued the initial intrusion by restraining defendant from being free to reenter her home. That show of authority, too, was a sufficient intrusion on defendant's liberty to constitute a seizure for purposes of Or. Const. art. I, § 9. However, the seizure of defendant was reasonable because officers believed that defendant's husband had just assaulted her. The officers acted reasonably in temporarily detaining defendant for purposes of questioning her as a witness to and victim of a recent or ongoing assault. The officers had an objectively reasonable basis to obtain and verify defendant's identity and an objectively reasonable belief that defendant could provide information material to the assault. The trial court therefore correctly denied defendant's motion to suppress evidence discovered in the subsequent consensual search of defendant.


OUTCOME: The judgment of the court of appeals was reversed. The judgment of the circuit court was affirmed.

Howell v. Boyle


SC S059120


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 359; 298 P.3d 1; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 184


September 8, 2011, Argued and Submitted; April 24, 2012, Reassigned 
March 14, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Howell v. Boyle, 2013 Ore. LEXIS 351 (Or., May 16, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
On certified questions from the United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit; certification order dated January 19, 2011; certification accepted February 17, 2011. US Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit 0936153.
Howell v. Boyle, 673 F.3d 1054, 2011 U.S. App. LEXIS 709 (9th Cir. Or., 2011)



DISPOSITION: Certified question answered.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff pedestrian sued defendants, a city and a police officer, in tort. The trial court found $1 million in damages, but reduced the award based on comparative fault. Defendants moved to reduce the award to the $200,000 limit of the Oregon Tort Claims Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 31.270(1)(b) (2007). The trial court denied the motion. On appeal, the United States Court of Appeals for the Ninth Circuit certified a question to the state supreme court.


OVERVIEW: In a personal injury case, plaintiff would have recovered $507,500 in economic and noneconomic damages but for the $200,000 damage limitation of the Oregon Tort Claims Act, Or. Rev. Stat. § 31.270(1)(b). The Ninth Circuit certified the following question to the Oregon Supreme Court: If plaintiff's action was protected by Or. Const. art. I, § 10, was $200,000 an unconstitutional emasculated remedy despite the jury's finding of comparative negligence? The court noted that the legislature had the authority to vary and modify both the form and the measure of recovery for an injury, so long as plaintiff was not left with less than a substantial remedy. The court held that the challenged $200,000 damage limitation did not leave plaintiff with a constitutionally inadequate remedy under Or. Const. art. I, § 10.


OUTCOME: The certified question was answered.

Doe v. Lake Oswego Sch. Dist.


SC S059589


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 321; 297 P.3d 1287; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 152


September 20, 2012, Argued and Submitted; January 7, 2013, Resubmitted 
March 7, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC CV-0802-0740; CA A140979. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Clackamas County Circuit Court, James C. Tait, Judge. 242 Ore. App. 605, 259 P.3d 27 (2011).


Doe v. Lake Oswego Sch. Dist., 242 Ore. App. 605, 259 P.3d 27, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 672 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The limited judgment of the circuit court is reversed, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiffs, former public school students, sued defendant district alleging that they were sexually abused by a fifth grade teacher between 1957 and 1970, but that they did not know that their teacher's touching was abusive when it occurred. The trial court granted the district's motion to dismiss, and the Court of Appeals, Oregon, affirmed. Plaintiffs sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Supreme Court of Oregon held that the action should not have been dismissed on timeliness grounds under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.275. Although it was true, as defendant argued, that in the 1970s and 1980s many fifth-graders would have known that the teacher's touching was offensive, plaintiffs alleged facts from which a jury could find that plaintiffs reasonably did not reach that conclusion at the time of the teacher's actions. Plaintiffs alleged that the teacher engaged in a grooming process that included gaining the support of their families so that they would counsel their sons to respect the teacher's authority and comply with his instructions and requests. Plaintiffs alleged that, as a result, they had such admiration and respect for the teacher, and the wrongful touching in which the teacher engaged was so similar to the non-tortious touching that they had experienced during the grooming process that, as young boys, they were confused by the teacher's conduct and unable to discern that the touching was inappropriate.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and the limited judgment of the trial court and remanded the case to the circuit court with directions.


 

44 of 770 DOCUMENTS


Crystal Communs., Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue


SC S059271


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 300; 297 P.3d 1256; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 149


September 18, 2012, Argued and Submitted; January 7, 2013, Resubmitted 
March 7, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
TC 4769. On appeal from the Oregon Tax Court. Henry C. Breithaupt, Judge.
Crystal Communs., Inc. v. Dep't of Revenue, 2010 Ore. Tax LEXIS 207 (Or. T.C., July 19, 2010)



DISPOSITION: The judgment of the Tax Court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Appellants Florida taxpayers sought review in the Oregon Tax Court of the decision of respondent Oregon Department of Revenue (department) reclassifying a gain from their sale of business assets as apportionable business income. The Court granted summary judgment in favor of the department, and the taxpayers appealed.


OVERVIEW: The taxpayers said the gain was not "business income" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 314.610(1) (1999) and not subject to allocation under Or. Rev. Stat. § 314.280 (1999). The supreme court held the department reasonably interpreted business income definitions in Or. Admin. R. 150-314.280-(B) (1999) because, by interpreting the Uniform Division of Income for Tax Purposes Act, Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 314.605 to 314.675 (1999), definition of business income in the Rule consistently with a California Supreme Court decision, the department gave effect to both definitions of business income in the Rule. The department was properly granted summary judgment because, so construed, both definitions of business income were broad enough to reach the gain from the sale of the corporate assets. The court's interpretation of Or. Admin. R. 150-314.280-(B) (1999) was consistent with Or. Rev. Stat. § 314.280 (1999) because (1) the statute's wording was broad enough to reach the department's reading of the Rule, allowing the department to apportion income derived from property used in the taxpayer's unitary business, and (2) nothing in the statute barred apportioning gain from assets sold in liquidation.


OUTCOME: The trial court's judgment was affirmed.

State v. Harrell

State v. Wilson, 240 Ore. App. 708, 247 P.3d 1262, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 150 (2011)
State v. Harrell, 241 Ore. App. 139, 250 P.3d 1, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 174 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decisions of the Court of Appeals are reversed. The cases are remanded to the circuit courts for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Defendants who unsuccessfully attempted to waive their right to a jury trial under Or. Const. art. I, § 11 appealed their convictions. The Oregon Court of Appeals affirmed. Defendants appealed.


OVERVIEW: Supreme court held that remand was appropriate for reconsideration of defendant one's waiver of a jury trial because it was difficult to determine whether the trial judge's refusal to consent to defendant one's exercise of his right to waive a jury was premised on a belief that the trial judge lacked authority to exercise discretion to consent to the waiver, or he believed he could not consider the waiver without a prosecutor's consent, or he had concluded that defendant's requested waiver was inconsistent with considerations of judicial economy. The court further held that remand was appropriate for reconsideration of defendant two's waiver of a jury trial; the trial court erred because it withheld its consent to defendant two's jury trial waiver based solely on the prosecutor's perceived objection -- a position that was not based on considerations of speed, economy, or the protection of defendant two's constitutional rights.

Morgan v. Sisters Sch. Dist. #6


SC S059465


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 189; 301 P.3d 419; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 5


March 5, 2012, Argued and Submitted 
January 17, 2013, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 08-CV-0423AB; CA A1422523. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Deschutes County Circuit Court Alta Jean Brady, Judge. 241 Or App 483, 251 P3d 207 (2011).


Morgan v. Sisters Sch. Dist. #6, 241 Ore. App. 483, 251 P.3d 207, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 330 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Petitioner on review taxpayer challenged a decision from the Court of Appeals (Oregon), which affirmed the circuit court's dismissal, based on lack of standing, of the taxpayer's suit for declaratory and injunctive relief alleging that respondent on review, a school district and its board of directors, lacked authority to issue certain obligations to finance improvements to district property without voter approval.


OVERVIEW: The district issued the obligations pursuant to a board resolution. The taxpayer alleged in his complaint that he had standing as a taxpayer and voter because the issuance of the obligations increased the likelihood that the district would seek additional funds from taxpayers and because he had been deprived of the right to vote on their issuance. He did not ask for a declaration that the obligations were invalid, nor did he request an order compelling the district to hold an election. Rather, he sought an order declaring that the district should have held an election and requiring the district to default on the obligations. The court held that the taxpayer lacked standing under Or. Rev. Stat. § 28.020 to seek relief under the Uniform Declaratory Judgments Act. As to voter standing, although denial of the right to vote could satisfy the personal injury requirement for standing, the requested declaration would have no practical effect on voting rights and would amount to a purely advisory opinion. As to taxpayer standing, the possibility of higher taxes was predicated on a series of hypothetical contingencies. The same analysis also applied to the claim for injunctive relief.


OUTCOME: The court affirmed the decision of the court of appeals and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

State v. Hemenway


SC S059085 (Control), S059392 (Consolidated)


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 129; 295 P.3d 617; 2013 Ore. LEXIS 3


November 14, 2011, Argued and Submitted at Reynolds High School, Troutdale, Oregon 
January 10, 2013, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Vacated by, Reconsideration dismissed by, As moot State v. Hemenway, 353 Ore. 498, 2013 Ore. LEXIS 323 (Or., Apr. 25, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 071107; CA A136981. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Tillamook County Circuit Court, Rick W. Roll, Judge. 232 Ore. App. 407, 222 P3d 1103 (2009).


State v. Hemenway, 232 Ore. App. 407, 222 P.3d 1103, 2009 Ore. App. LEXIS 1954 (2009)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed. The judgment of the circuit court is affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In trial for possession of methamphetamine, the trial court denied defendant's motion to suppress under Or. Const. art. I, § 9, and defendant entered a conditional guilty plea. The Court of Appeals, Oregon, reversed. The State sought further review.


OVERVIEW: The Court of Appeals held that evidence obtained through exploitation of an unlawful stop should have been suppressed. The Supreme Court of Oregon articulated and applied a clarified test for exploitation, disavowing the minimal factual nexus part of the Hall test, and held that suppression was not required under Or. Const. art. I, § 9. Defendant's consent to search his pockets was not the product of the unlawful stop because defendant consented in order to ease the mind of the officer, who was concerned because defendant had his hands in his pockets, which were bulky, and had weapons in his vehicle, and it was very dark at the location. Drug evidence from a search of a tin found in defendant's pocket was not tainted by the unlawful stop because the search of defendant's pocket was valid and there was no indication that the officer exploited the stop to gain defendant's consent to open the tin. Defendant's voluntary consent to search his house following his arrest was valid because evidence from the prior two searches gave the officer probable cause to arrest defendant, and defendant was given Miranda warnings before the officer requested consent.


OUTCOME: The court reversed the decision of the Court of Appeals and affirmed the judgment of the circuit court.

Rachel M. Weldon, LPC v. Bd. of Licensed Prof'l Counselors & Therapists


SC S060483


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 85; 293 P.3d 1023; 2012 Ore. LEXIS 840


October 10, 2012, Argued and Submitted 
December 20, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Decision reached on appeal by, Remanded by Weldon v. Bd. of Licensed Prof'l Counselors & Therapists, 266 Ore. App. 52, 337 P.3d 911, 2014 Ore. App. LEXIS 1367 (2014)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
BLPCT 2009026; CA A151028. On review of an order of the Court of Appeals.*


* Order Granting Reconsideration and Modifying Order Denying Stay, dated June 1, 2012.


Weldon v. Bd. of Licensed Prof'l Counselors & Therapists, 2012 Ore. App. LEXIS 1620 (Or. Ct. App., June 1, 2012)



DISPOSITION: The order of the Court of Appeals is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: The Oregon Court of Appeals denied petitioner therapist's motion for a stay and vacated that part of the Appellate Commissioner's order that had permitted the therapist to file a supersedeas undertaking to stay respondent Board of Licensed Professional Counselors and Therapists' (board) monetary assessments. The therapist petitioned for review.


OVERVIEW: The supreme court noted that the parties presented the issue of whether the court of appeals had authority to grant a stay as one of constitutional magnitude. The supreme court concluded from the text, context, and legislative history of Or. Rev. Stat. § 676.210 that the legislature's purpose in enacting that statute was to grant courts statutory power to enter injunctions, not to deprive them of their inherent judicial power to enter stays. Section 676.210 made a board's order suspending or revoking a health care practitioner's license immediately effective and granted a court authority to enforce it, but also permitted a board and a court acting pursuant to the Administrative Procedures Act to stay an order of suspension or revocation of license pending appeal. The board went astray when it argued, and the court of appeals erred in deciding, that § 676.210 deprived the Court of Appeals of authority to issue a stay pending its decision on the merits of the therapist's appeal.


OUTCOME: The judgment was reversed and remanded to the court of appeals for further proceedings.

State v. Marsh & McLennan Cos.


SC S059386


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


353 Ore. 1; 292 P.3d 525; 2012 Ore. LEXIS 833


December 7, 2011, Argued and Submitted 
December 13, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: On remand at, Remanded by State v. Marsh & McLennan Cos., 2015 Ore. App. LEXIS 145 (Or. Ct. App., Feb. 11, 2015)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 050808454; CA A139453. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Multnomah County Circuit Court, Frank L. Bearden, Judge. 241 Ore. App. 107, 250 P3d 371 (2011).


State v. Marsh & McLennan Cos., 241 Ore. App. 107, 250 P.3d 371, 2011 Ore. App. LEXIS 172 (2011)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals is reversed, and the case is remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: In a securities fraud action brought by plaintiff buyer, the State of Oregon, the Oregon Court of Appeals affirmed a trial court's grant of summary judgment in favor of defendant seller, finding that Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.135 and Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.137 required proof of reliance on misrepresentations and rejecting the buyer's fraud on the market claim. The buyer appealed.


OVERVIEW: The State purchased more than $ 15 million of common stock in the seller in the open market on the New York Stock Exchange (NYSE) in 2003 and 2004. The State alleged that the seller's shares were traded on an efficient securities market, that the price of the shares reflected the material information that the seller disclosed to the market, and that the price of the shares was artificially inflated because of misrepresentations made by the seller, including false representations that the seller had complied with a strict ethical code of conduct and concealing the fact that the seller's reported financial results were achieved through unethical and illegal business practices. The court held that the State was required to establish reliance as an element of its fraud claim. The fraud on the market theory was applicable in Oregon because the U.S. Supreme Court case adopting that theory was decided in 1988, and Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.137 was enacted in 2003. Consequently, by the time Oregon enacted Or. Rev. Stat. § 59.137, the fraud-on-the-market doctrine had been part of the federal law landscape for 15 years.


OUTCOME: The decision of the Court of Appeals was reversed, and the case was remanded to the Court of Appeals for further proceedings.

State v. Rogers


SC S053466


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


352 Ore. 510; 288 P.3d 544; 2012 Ore. LEXIS 745


January 12, 2012, Argued and Submitted 
October 11, 2012, Filed


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 88-355, 88-356, 88-357, 88-359, 88-360. On automatic and direct review of the sentence of death imposed by the Clackamas County Circuit Court. Ronald D. Thom, Judge.
State v. Rogers, 334 Ore. 633, 55 P.3d 488, 2002 Ore. LEXIS 672 (2002)



DISPOSITION: The sentence of death is vacated, and the case is remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: A jury in the Clackamas County Circuit Court (Oregon) imposed the death sentence on defendant for aggravated murder. Review was automatic and direct.


OVERVIEW: Defendant argued that the amendment to Or. Const. art. I, § 40, to allow the death penalty, made more than one substantive change to the Oregon Constitution and therefore violated Or. Const. art. XVII, § 1, which required a separate vote for separate amendments. The court held that although several changes were made to facilitate permitting the death penalty, those changes were closely related, so that the measure did not violate the separate vote requirement. The court held, however, that the trial court erred in empaneling an anonymous jury. The trial court adopted a procedure that expressly precluded defendant from learning the names and addresses of jurors. Although the trial court made an effort to explain that there was a non-prejudicial reason for the deviation from the norm, that they were being permitted to withhold information to protect their anonymity from the public and the press, it also told eight of the 12 jurors that it would furnish their names, not to "the parties," but to "the attorneys," implying that defendant was dangerous. The explanation for permitting anonymity did not negate the risk to juror impartiality that the unusual anonymity procedure posed.


OUTCOME: The sentence of death was vacated, and the case was remanded to the circuit court for further proceedings.

Hazell v. Brown


SC S059245 (Control), S059246


SUPREME COURT OF OREGON


352 Ore. 455; 287 P.3d 1079; 2012 Ore. LEXIS 742


January 9, 2012, Argued and Submitted 
October 4, 2012, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Reconsideration denied by Hazell v. Brown, 2013 Ore. LEXIS 484 (Or., June 20, 2013)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 
CC 06C22473; CA A137397. On review from the Court of Appeals. *


* Appeal from Marion County Circuit Court, Mary Mertens James, Judge. 238 Ore. App. 487, 242 P3d 743 (2010).


Hazell v. Brown, 238 Ore. App. 487, 242 P.3d 743, 2010 Ore. App. LEXIS 1295 (2010)



DISPOSITION: The decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court are affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


PROCEDURAL POSTURE: Plaintiff voters sought review of a decision of the Oregon Court of Appeals affirming a trial court's decision denying declaratory and injunctive relief to compel the State to enforce Or. Ballot Measure 47 (2006), Or. Rev. Stat. ch. 259, which required creation of new campaign finance statutes to implement Or. Ballot Measure 46, which was simultaneously rejected when Measure 47 was approved by Oregon voters.


OVERVIEW: Measure 46 (2006) sought to amend the Oregon Constitution to permit the enactment of laws prohibiting or limiting electoral campaign contributions and expenditures. Measure 47 (2006) sought to create new campaign finance statutes that would implement Measure 46. The State took the position that Measure 47 was unenforceable because Measure 46 was defeated. Intervenors asserted that Measure 47 was unconstitutional. The supreme court concluded that Measure 47 was enforceable because § 9(f) required Measure 47 to be codified and held in abeyance pending an appropriate constitutional amendment or judicial decision that would render it operative. In addition, § 9(f) did not violate Or. Const. art. I, § 21 because it's taking effect did not depend on any authority. Finally, the supreme court ruled that it could not rule on the constitutionality of Measure 47 because plaintiffs neglected to allege a justiciable controversy under the declaratory judgment act as to the individual provisions of Measure 47.


OUTCOME: The supreme court affirmed the decision of the Court of Appeals and the judgment of the circuit court.
