Bell v. City of Hood River


A156481


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


283 Ore. App. 13; 388 P.3d 1128; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1612


June 15, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
December 21, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Hood River County Circuit Court. 120088CC. John A Olson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Vacated and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Or. Const. art. I, § 10, did not apply to the city's fee because the city's fee did not pose a direct bar to plaintiffs' access to the courts, and plaintiffs had expressly decided not to assert that the city was acting as a court administering justice when it charged the fee; the court erred by dismissing plaintiffs' declaratory judgment action instead of entering a judgment that declared the parties' respective rights.


OUTCOME: Judgment vacated and case remanded.

Migis v. AutoZone, Inc.


A150540


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


282 Ore. App. 774; 387 P.3d 381; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1591


January 6, 2015, Argued and Submitted, on respondent's motion for reconsideration filed May 24, 2012, and appellant's response to motion to reconsider order filed June 7, 2012. 
December 14, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Affirmed by, On reconsideration by Migis v. Autozone, Inc., 2017 Ore. App. LEXIS 792 (Or. Ct. App., June 21, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Multnomah County Circuit Court. 071113531. Jerome E. LaBarre, Judge.
Migis v. Autozone, Inc., 2013 Ore. LEXIS 28 (Or., Jan. 24, 2013)



DISPOSITION: Reconsideration of order of Appellate Commissioner denying motion to dismiss allowed; previous order denying motion to dismiss adhered to. On appeal, (1) general judgment reversed and remanded as to off-the-clock claim penalties; otherwise affirmed; (2) supplemental judgment reversed and remanded. On cross-appeal, affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court did not err in denying motions to decertify a class of employees claiming off-the-clock work because an alleged policy or practice supported a finding of commonality under Or. R. Civ. P. 32(A) and the assessment of superiority under Rule 32(B) was not necessarily determined by the issue of predominance, which could properly have been found in any event; [2]-The imposition of civil penalties under Or. Rev. Stat. § 653.055(1), incorporating by reference Or. Rev. Stat. § 652.150, required establishing that the employer's failure to pay wages was willful; [3]-Reversal as to penalties required that a supplemental judgment for attorney fees be reversed and remanded under Or. Rev. Stat. § 20.220(3); on remand, attorney fees could not be awarded under Or. Rev. Stat. § 652.200(2) because a prelitigation notice letter that failed to name the plaintiff was deficient.


OUTCOME: Reversed in part and remanded.

 

181 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Stewart


A160496


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


282 Ore. App. 845; 386 P.3d 688; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1553


September 28, 2016, Argued and Submitted 
December 14, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Stewart, 361 Ore. 311, 2017 Ore. LEXIS 258 (Or., Mar. 31, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 15CR14797. Marion County Circuit Court. Susan M. Tripp, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Portion of judgment requiring defendant to pay attorney fees reversed; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In a prosecution for unlawful delivery of methamphetamine, there was sufficient evidence for purposes of sentencing to support a finding that the delivery was "for consideration" under Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.900(2)(a) because evidence that defendant was dividing methamphetamine into separate baggies while stating he needed to make some money supported a finding that he possessed the methamphetamine with the intent to exchange it for money; it was not necessary to prove that he actually entered into an agreement to receive consideration or completed a drug transaction in exchange for consideration; [2]-Attorney fees should not have been imposed in the absence of evidence concerning defendant's financial resources.


OUTCOME: Reversed in part; affirmed in part.

 

182 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Ambill


A154252


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


282 Ore. App. 821; 385 P.3d 1110; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1588


November 25, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
December 14, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by State v. Ambill, 2017 Ore. LEXIS 309 (Or., Apr. 27, 2017)
Review denied by State v. Ambill, 2017 Ore. LEXIS 411 (Or., June 1, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Coos County Circuit Court. 12CR0830. Martin E. Stone, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed on appeal and cross-appeal.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant's sentence for murder of a 25-year minimum term without eligibility for parole was proper in accordance with Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115(5)(a) and (b); the court rejected the State's contention that the trial court was required to impose the guidelines sentence under Or. Rev. Stat. § 137.637 if the trial court determined that the sentence under the guidelines exceeded 25 years; [2]-Examining the text, context, and legislative history of Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.115 persuaded the court that the legislature intended an offender convicted of murder to be sentenced to an indeterminate life sentence with the 25-year minimum term of incarceration specified in § 163.115(5)(b), and that the legislature did not intend for a sentencing court to impose a different minimum term of incarceration under the guidelines or any other source of law.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. J. J.-M. (In re J. J.-M.)


A155910


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


282 Ore. App. 459; 387 P.3d 426; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1509


October 13, 2015, Submitted 
November 30, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] J1102501; Petition Number J1102502. Hood River County Circuit Court. John A. Olson, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Counsel was not ineffective under U.S. Const. amend. VI for failing to obtain a handwriting analysis because retaining a handwriting expert to show that the handwriting was affirmatively not defendant's would neither rebut the prosecution's evidence nor the prosecution's theory of the case; the prosecution had no evidence that the handwriting on the back of the birth certificate was defendant's handwriting; [2]-Counsel was not ineffective under U.S. Const. amend. VI for failing to interview a witness because the testimony about another person's statements would have been inadmissible hearsay, and defendant did not identify any hearsay exception that would have permitted the witness's testimony; further, defendant failed to provide evidence of what the declarant's testimony would have been had he been called as a witness and the resulting impact of that testimony.


OUTCOME: The judgment was affirmed.

187 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Schindler


A154305


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


281 Ore. App. 86; 381 P.3d 973; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1091


August 27, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
September 14, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 121189. Tillamook County Circuit Court. Jonathan R. Hill, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Prior to his trial for using a child in a display of sexually explicit conduct, Or. Rev. Stat. § 163.670, defendant raised the issue of venue by first filing a motion to suppress and then, when he was successful, moving to dismiss on the basis that the State would not be able to prove venue; this was not consistent with the procedure required by State v. Mills; [2]-Although claiming the State would not be able to prove that his requests for the victim to send nude photos occurred in Tillamook County, he never suggested that Tillamook was, in fact, not the proper place for the charges against him to proceed, nor did he ask for an evidentiary hearing; [3]-Even if the evidence presented would not permit a finding that defendant was in Tillamook County at the pertinent times, venue would be proper in Tillamook because that was defendant's county of residence.


OUTCOME: Judgment reversed and case remanded for an evidentiary hearing on venue.

 

188 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Villagomez


A156397


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


281 Ore. App. 29; 380 P.3d 1150; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1082


January 27, 2016, Argued and submitted 
September 14, 2016, Filed


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by State v. Villagomez, 2017 Ore. LEXIS 84 (Or., Feb. 2, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Yamhill County Circuit Court. 13CR08907. Cynthia L. Easterday, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction on Count 2 reversed and remanded for entry of judgment of conviction for possession of a controlled substance without the commercial drug offense enhancement; remanded for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Evidence was insufficient to support a commercial drug offense enhancement under Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.900(1)(b) because there was no proof that consideration for the delivery had been tendered or arranged; although defendant had $4,395 in cash when he was arrested, there was no evidence that the money was payment for the drugs; [2]-The denial of defendant's motion for judgment of acquittal was harmless error as to delivery because of another enhancement finding, but not as to possession; [3]-To prove that a delivery was "for consideration" within the meaning § 475.900(1)(b)(A), the state must show that the defendant has received, or has an entered into an agreement to receive, some benefit from or detriment incurred by another person at the time that he or she commits a delivery; that is so whether the delivery is an actual, attempted, or constructive transfer.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded in part; affirmed in part.

 

189 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Rankins


A154629


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


280 Ore. App. 673; 382 P.3d 530; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1072


February 26, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
September 8, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Lane County Circuit Court. 201209098. Josephine H. Mooney, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction on Count 1 reversed and remanded for entry of judgment of conviction for delivery of a controlled substance without the commercial drug offense enhancement; remanded for resentencing; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Text messages that related to drug transactions and were sent and received by defendant were not "drug transaction records" for purposes of the commercial sales enhancement under Or. Rev. Stat. § 475.900(1)(b)(E) because the text messages were created only hours before they were discovered, were limited in number, and were not stored in an organized fashion; any inference that defendant had the text messages for record-keeping purposes would have been speculative, and the record did not support an inference that they were anything other than the detritus of digital communications; [2]-The term "records" means intentionally retained notations regarding events, and the term "drug transaction records" applies to notations similar to business records, that is, records maintained in furtherance of an enterprise conducted over a period of time.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded in part; affirmed in part.

OUTCOME: Appeal dismissed.

Mann v. DeCamp


A152797


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


280 Ore. App. 427; 380 P.3d 1080; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 1040


May 8, 2015, Submitted 
August 31, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Mann v. DeCamp, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 758 (Or., Dec. 8, 2016)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 12C16717. Marion County Circuit Court. Lindsay R. Partridge, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Petitioner inmate's post-conviction relief petition was properly dismissed as untimely under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.510(3) and impermissibly successive under Or. Rev. Stat. § 138.550(3) because, when he claimed his convictions were entered by a judge without such authority, he actually contested the adequacy of his representation, which was not exempt from Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.510(3) and 138.550(3), and, even if the judge lacked authority to preside over his trial, this would only show his convictions were voidable and subject to Or. Rev. Stat. §§ 138.510(3) and 138.550(3).


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Conrad

August 24, 2016, Decided

State v. Davilla


A153461


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


280 Ore. App. 43; 380 P.3d 1003; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 969


February 10, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
August 3, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] CR9200004. Clackamas County Circuit Court. Eve L. Miller, Judge.
State v. Davilla, 121 Ore. App. 583, 855 P.2d 1160, 1993 Ore. App. LEXIS 1170 (1993)



DISPOSITION: Remanded for resentencing.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-In resentencing defendant for a 1991 murder, the trial court improperly imposed an upward departure of 600 months' imprisonment because the departure was based in part on factors other than defendant's use of a dangerous weapon, the only aggravating factor that the state proved at trial, as required by Or. Rev. Stat. § 136.765; [2]-To the extent the departure was based on use of a dangerous weapon, the trial court's explanation regarding defendant's choice of a small, dull knife and the increased pain and suffering experienced by the victim was insufficient to demonstrate why defendant's use of a dangerous weapon justified the departure; [3]-Or. Admin. R. 213-008-0002(2) did not preclude defendant's use of a dangerous weapon as an aggravating factor that could justify a departure sentence because use of a dangerous weapon was not a statutory element of murder.


OUTCOME: Remanded for resentencing.

Hessel v. Dep't of Corr.


A148471


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


280 Ore. App. 16; 380 P.3d 1048; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 966


March 31, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
August 3, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review denied by Hessel v. Dep't of Corr., 2017 Ore. LEXIS 284 (Or., Apr. 13, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Department of Corrections.



DISPOSITION: OAR 291-105-0005(3)(d), OAR 291-105-0010(29), and OAR 291-105-0015(4)(n) held valid.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Administrative rules could be applied retroactively, without referring to the need for express authorization from the legislature to adopt such rules, and Or. Admin. R. 291-105-0005(3)(d) was consistent with state law because it clearly stated the Department of Corrections' intention to apply it retroactively; [2]-Or. Admin. R. 291-105-0010(29) was valid under the department's broad grant of authority from the legislature to adopt rules pertaining to inmate misconduct; [3]-Defining "order" to include "all federal, state and local laws" was not so indeterminate as to allow for ad hoc judgments as the phrase "all federal, state and local laws" was capable of precise identification as to what was included; [4]-The appellate court did not address the inmates' challenge to Or. Admin. R. 291-105-0015(4)(n).


OUTCOME: Rules are valid.

 

195 of 770 DOCUMENTS


State v. Hirschman


A153610


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


279 Ore. App. 338; 379 P.3d 616; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 894


December 23, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
July 7, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Deschutes County Circuit Court. MI121020. A. Michael Adler, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Reversed and remanded.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendant violated Or. Rev. Stat. § 260.715(9) when he posted on online advertisement stating that he would give $20 to a person who would bring the person's official ballot to defendant, let defendant complete it, then sign the person's own name and submit the ballot to an elections volunteer; a person "offers to purchase any official ballot," for purposes of § 260.715(9), if the person communicates a message that objectively would be understood as proposing to purchase the right to use another person's ballot; [2]-The statutory prohibition on making an offer to purchase a ballot is facially unconstitutional because, by its terms, it criminalizes expression and is not wholly contained within a well-established historical exception to the protections of Or. Const. art. I, § 8; defendant's demurrer to a charge of violating that statute should have been granted.


OUTCOME: Reversed and remanded.

Hardin v. Popoff

COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON

Cruz v. Multnomah Cnty.


A155157


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


279 Ore. App. 1; 381 P.3d 856; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 785


November 7, 2014, Argued and Submitted 
June 22, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 120911181. Multnomah County Circuit Court. Stephen K. Bushong, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-Defendants were immune from liability under Or. Rev. Stat. § 30.265(6)(f) because they acted under the "apparent authority" of 8 C.F.R. § 287.7(d); defendants' construction of § 287.7(d) was plausible, as it was based on the text of the regulation, relied on an ordinary meaning of the word "shall," and was part of a coherent construction of the regulation as a whole; [2]-The trial court correctly concluded that plaintiff's claim under Or. Rev. Stat. § 181A.820(1) failed as a matter of law because the legislature's intention was not to create a statutory tort for violation of the duty imposed by the statute; the legislature's intention was to reduce the potential liability of law enforcement agencies under existing law by expressly prohibiting problematic activities, and not to create additional liability through creation of a new statutory tort.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

State v. Wade


A156163


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


278 Ore. App. 669; 377 P.3d 660; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 722


December 16, 2015, Argued and Submitted 
June 8, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Multnomah County Circuit Court. 130546222. Eric J. Bergstrom, Judge.



DISPOSITION: Conviction for disorderly conduct reversed; otherwise affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The evidence was insufficient to support a conviction for second-degree disorderly conduct under Or. Rev. Stat. § 166.025(1)(a) because it did not support an inference that defendant's conduct (arching his pelvis, yelling incoherent obscenities, unfastening his pants, and reaching as though he was about to expose his genitals) was "immediately likely" to produce his use of physical force, given that he was unarmed and remained standing at a distance from the complainant, took no steps toward her, and did not otherwise indicate that he would begin closing the distance between them.


OUTCOME: Conviction for disorderly conduct reversed; otherwise affirmed.

Wittemyer v. City of Portland


A154844


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


278 Ore. App. 746; 377 P.3d 589; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 717


May 2, 2014, Submitted 
June 8, 2016, Decided


SUBSEQUENT HISTORY: Review granted by Wittemyer v. City of Portland, 360 Ore. 400, 381 P.3d 837, 2016 Ore. LEXIS 547 (Sept. 15, 2016)
Affirmed by Wittemyer v. City of Portland, 361 Ore. 854, 2017 Ore. LEXIS 639 (Sept. 21, 2017)


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] Multnomah County Circuit Court. 130304234. Kelly Skye, Judge.
Bogdanski v. City of Portland, 21 OTR 341, 2014 Ore. Tax LEXIS 13 (Jan. 28, 2014)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The City of Portland's tax of $35 on the income of each income-earning resident for support of the arts in the public schools is not a "poll or head tax" in violation of Or. Const. art. IX, § 1a because it incorporates financial exceptions, yielding diverse, income-predicated applications that contradict the fundamental per capita character of a poll or head tax; [2]-In 1910 "poll or head tax" for purposes of Or. Const. art. IX, § 1a had a precise and particular meaning that did not include measures with exemptions based on the amount or source of individual or household income.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.

Friends of Yamhill Cnty. v. Bd. of Cnty. Comm'rs of Yamhill Cnty.


A158505


COURT OF APPEALS OF OREGON


278 Ore. App. 472; 377 P.3d 670; 2016 Ore. App. LEXIS 619


March 22, 2016, Argued and Submitted 
May 25, 2016, Decided


PRIOR HISTORY:  [***1] 14CV10124. Yamhill County Circuit Court. Ronald W. Stone, Judge.
Biggerstaff v. Bd. of County Comm'r, 240 Ore. App. 46, 245 P.3d 688, 2010 Ore. App. LEXIS 1672 (2010)



DISPOSITION: Affirmed.


CASE SUMMARY:


OVERVIEW: HOLDINGS: [1]-The trial court correctly found that a writ of review was the exclusive means to obtain review over all parts of the 2014 vested rights decision, including the determination that the nonconforming use provision in the county's zoning ordinance did not apply to Measure 49 authorizations; [2]-The landowners' request directly sought to have the court review the vested rights decision for errors, but a request to correct an alleged error in a quasi-judicial decision was justiciable only by writ of review and not otherwise by means of a declaratory judgment proceeding.


OUTCOME: Judgment affirmed.
